# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes sig-node Kubelet Component Ownership Map

## Your Task

Map the major kubelet components in kubernetes/kubernetes owned by sig-node. Find the Go source files that implement: the pod lifecycle manager, the container runtime interface (CRI) client, the volume manager, and the device plugin manager.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [

  ],

  ],

    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully mapped the major kubelet components in kubernetes/kubernetes owned by sig-node. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary of Findings

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with comprehensive information about the four major kubelet components:

### 1. **Pod Lifecycle Manager**
- Located in `pkg/kubelet/lifecycle/`
- Key files: `interfaces.go` (defines interfaces), `handlers.go` (implements handler execution)
- Core interfaces: `PodAdmitHandler`, `PodSyncLoopHandler`, `PodSyncHandler`
- Manages pod admission, synchronization, and eviction decisions

### 2. **Container Runtime Interface (CRI) Client**
- Located in `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/`
- Main file: `kuberuntime_manager.go`
- Core struct: `kubeGenericRuntimeManager` (lines 98-179)
- Factory: `NewKubeGenericRuntimeManager()` (lines 189-222)
- Handles all container operations via gRPC CRI API

### 3. **Volume Manager**
- Located in `pkg/kubelet/volumemanager/`
- Main file: `volume_manager.go`
- Core struct: `volumeManager` (lines 242-250)
- Interface: `VolumeManager` (lines 93-158)
- Factory: `NewVolumeManager()` (lines 181-240)
- Manages attach/detach/mount/unmount operations

### 4. **Device Plugin Manager**
- Located in `pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager/`
- Main file: `plugin_manager.go`
- Core struct: `pluginManager` (lines 83-104)
- Interface: `PluginManager` (lines 35-44)
- Factory: `NewPluginManager()` (lines 54-80)
- Handles device plugin discovery and registration

All components are initialized and integrated in `pkg/kubelet/kubelet.go` within the `NewMainKubelet` function, forming the core of the Kubernetes node's pod lifecycle management system.

If no matching\n112: // port is found, an error is returned.\n113: func resolvePort(portReference intstr.IntOrString, container *v1.Container) (int, error) {\n114: \tif portReference.Type == intstr.Int {\n115: \t\treturn portReference.IntValue(), nil\n116: \t}\n117: \tportName := portReference.StrVal\n118: \tport, err := strconv.Atoi(portName)\n119: \tif err == nil {\n120: \t\treturn port, nil\n121: \t}\n122: \tfor _, portSpec := range container.Ports {\n123: \t\tif portSpec.Name == portName {\n124: \t\t\treturn int(portSpec.ContainerPort), nil\n125: \t\t}\n126: \t}\n127: \treturn -1, fmt.Errorf(\"couldn't find port: %v in %v\", portReference, container)\n128: }\n129: \n130: func (hr *handlerRunner) runSleepHandler(ctx context.Context, seconds int64) error {\n131: \tif !utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.PodLifecycleSleepAction) {\n132: \t\treturn nil\n133: \t}\n134: \tc := time.After(time.Duration(seconds) * time.Second)\n135: \tselect {\n136: \tcase <-ctx.Done():\n137: \t\t// unexpected termination\n138: \t\tmetrics.LifecycleHandlerSleepTerminated.Inc()\n139: \t\treturn fmt.Errorf(\"container terminated before sleep hook finished\")\n140: \tcase <-c:\n141: \t\treturn nil\n142: \t}\n143: }\n144: \n145: func (hr *handlerRunner) runHTTPHandler(ctx context.Context, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container, handler *v1.LifecycleHandler, eventRecorder record.EventRecorder) error {\n146: \thost := handler.HTTPGet.Host\n147: \tpodIP := host\n148: \tif len(host) == 0 {\n149: \t\tstatus, err := hr.containerManager.GetPodStatus(ctx, pod.UID, pod.Name, pod.Namespace)\n150: \t\tif err != nil {\n151: ",
